v2">\n<span>By</span>\n\t\t<ul>\n\t\t<li>\n\t\t\t\t\t<a href="https://www.techtarget.com/contributor/Ben-Lutkevich">Ben Lutkevich,</a>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<span class="main-article-author-title">Technical Writer</span>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t</li> \n\t\t<li>\n\t\t\t\t\t<a href="https://www.techtarget.com/contributor/Jack-Vaughan">Jack Vaughan,</a>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<span class="main-article-author-title">Senior News Writer</span>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t</li> \n\t\t</ul>\t\n\t</div>\n</section>\t\t<section class="section definition-section" data-menu-title="Definition" id="content-body">\n<section class="section main-article-chapter" data-menu-title="What is a data engineer?">\n <h3 class="section-title"><i class="icon" data-icon="1"></i>What is a data engineer?</h3>\n <p>A data engineer is an IT worker whose primary job is to prepare data for analytical or operational uses. These software engineers are typically responsible for building data pipelines to bring together information from different source systems. They integrate, consolidate and <a href="https://searchdatamanagement.techtarget.com/definition/data-scrubbing">cleanse data</a> and structure it for use in analytics applications. They aim to make data easily accessible and to optimize their organization\'s <a href="https://searchdatamanagement.techtarget.com/definition/big-data">big data</a> ecosystem.</p>\n <p>The amount of data an engineer works with varies with the organization, particularly with respect to its size. The bigger the company, the more complex the analytics architecture, and the <a href="https://searchdatamanagement.techtarget.com/definition/big-data-engineer">more data the engineer</a> will be responsible for. Certain industries are more data-intensive, including healthcare, retail and financial services.</p>\n <p>Data engineers work in conjunction with data science teams, <a href="https://searchcio.techtarget.com/feature/The-future-of-trust-must-be-built-on-data-transparency">improving data transparency</a> and enabling businesses to make more trustworthy business decisions.</p>\n <figure class="main-article-image full-col" data-img-fullsize="https://cdn.ttgtmedia.com/rms/onlineimages/data_management-comparing_roles.png">\n  <img data-src="https://cdn.ttgtmedia.com/rms/onlineimages/data_management-comparing_roles_mobile.png" class="lazy" data-srcset="https://cdn.ttgtmedia.com/rms/onlineimages/data_management-comparing_roles_mobile.png 960w,https://cdn.ttgtmedia.com/rms/onlineimages/data_management-comparing_roles_desktop.png 1280w" alt="how data management jobs compare">\n  <figcaption>\n   <i class="icon pictures" data-icon="z"></i>See how eight different data management jobs stack up against one another other.\n  </figcaption>\n  <div class="main-article-image-enlarge">\n   <i class="icon" data-icon="w"></i>\n  </div>\n </figure>\n</section>     \n<section class="section main-article-chapter" data-menu-title="The data engineer role">\n <h3 class="section-title"><i class="icon" data-icon="1"></i>The data engineer role</h3>\n <p>Data engineers focus on collecting and preparing data for use by <a href="https://searchenterpriseai.techtarget.com/definition/data-scientist">data scientists</a> and analysts. They take on three main roles as follows:</p>\n <ul class="default-list"> \n  <li><strong> Generalists.&nbsp;</strong>Data engineers with a general focus typically work on small teams, doing end-to-end data collection, intake and processing. They may have more skill than most data engineers, but less knowledge of systems architecture. A data scientist looking to become a data engineer would fit well into the generalist role.</li> \n </ul>\n <p style="padding-left: 30px;">A project a generalist data engineer might undertake for a small, metro-area food delivery service would be to create a <a href="https://searchbusinessanalytics.techtarget.com/definition/business-intelligence-dashboard">dashboard</a> that displays the number of deliveries made each day for the past month and forecasts the delivery volume for the following month.</p>\n <ul class="default-list"> \n  <li><strong>Pipeline-centric engineers. </strong>These data engineers typically work on a midsize data analytics team and more complicated data science projects across distributed systems. Midsize and large companies are more likely to need this role.</li> \n </ul>\n <p style="padding-left: 30px;">A regional food delivery company might undertake a pipeline-centric project to create a tool for data scientists and analysts to search <a href="https://whatis.techtarget.com/definition/metadata">metadata</a> for information about deliveries. They might look at distance driven and drive time required for deliveries in the past month, then use that data in a predictive algorithm to see what it means for the company\'s future business.</p>\n <ul class="default-list"> \n  <li><strong>Database-centric engineers.</strong> These data engineers are tasked with implementing, maintaining and populating analytics databases. This role typically exists at larger companies where data is distributed across several databases. The engineers work with pipelines, tune databases for efficient analysis and create table schemas using extract, transform, load (<a href="https://searchdatamanagement.techtarget.com/definition/Extract-Load-Transform-ELT">ETL</a>) methods. ETL is a process in which data is copied from several sources into a single destination system.</li> \n </ul>\n <p style="padding-left: 30px;">A database-centric project at a large, multistate or national food delivery service would be to design an analytics database. In addition to creating the database, the data engineer would write the code to get data from where it\'s collected in the main application database into the analytics database.</p>\n</section>        \n<section class="section main-article-chapter" data-menu-title="Data engineer responsibilities">\n <h3 class="section-title"><i class="icon" data-icon="1"></i>Data engineer responsibilities</h3>\n <p>Data engineers often work as part of an analytics team alongside data scientists. The engineers provide data in usable formats to the data scientists who run queries and algorithms against the information for predictive analytics, <a href="https://searchenterpriseai.techtarget.com/definition/machine-learning-ML">machine learning</a> and data mining applications. Data engineers also deliver aggregated data to business executives and analysts and other end users so they can analyze it and apply the results to improving business operations.</p>\n <figure class="main-article-image full-col" data-img-fullsize="https://cdn.ttgtmedia.com/rms/onlineImages/data_management-data_analytics.png">\n  <img data-src="https://cdn.ttgtmedia.com/rms/onlineImages/data_management-data_analytics_mobile.png" class="lazy" data-srcset="https://cdn.ttgtmedia.com/rms/onlineImages/data_management-data_analytics_mobile.png 960w,https://cdn.ttgtmedia.com/rms/onlineImages/data_management-data_analytics_desktop.png 1280w" alt="data engineer and data scientist responsibilities on a data analytics team">\n  <figcaption>\n   <i class="icon pictures" data-icon="z"></i>Data engineers and data scientists contribute different skills to the data analytics team.\n  </figcaption>\n  <div class="main-article-image-enlarge">\n   <i class="icon" data-icon="w"></i>\n  </div>\n </figure>\n <p>Data engineers deal with both <a href="https://searchcontentmanagement.techtarget.com/tip/Challenges-of-combining-structured-and-unstructured-data">structured and unstructured data</a>. Structured data is information that can be organized into a formatted repository like a database. Unstructured data -- such as text, images, audio and video files -- doesn\'t conform to conventional data models. Data engineers must understand different approaches to data architecture and applications to handle both data types. A variety of big data technologies, such as open source data ingestion and processing frameworks, are also part of the data engineer\'s toolkit.</p>\n</section>    \n<section class="section main-article-chapter" data-menu-title="Data engineer skill set">\n <h3 class="section-title"><i class="icon" data-icon="1"></i>Data engineer skill set</h3>\n <p>Data engineers are skilled in programming languages such as C#, Java, Python, R, Ruby, Scala and SQL. Python, R and SQL are the three most important languages data engineers use.</p>\n <p>Engineers need a good understanding of ETL tools and <a href="https://searchapparchitecture.techtarget.com/definition/REST-REpresentational-State-Transfer">REST-oriented APIs</a> for creating and managing data integration jobs. These skills also help in providing data analysts and business users with simplified access to prepared data sets.</p>\n <p>Data engineers must understand data warehouses and data lakes and how they work. For instance, <a href="https://searchdatamanagement.techtarget.com/definition/Hadoop-data-lake">Hadoop data lakes</a> that offload the processing and storage work of established enterprise data warehouses support the big data analytics efforts data engineers work on.</p>\n <p>Data engineers must also understand NoSQL databases and Apache Spark systems, which are becoming common components of data workflows. Data engineers should have a knowledge of relational database systems as well, such as MySQL and PostgreSQL. Another focus is <a href="https://searchbusinessanalytics.techtarget.com/definition/Lambda-architecture">Lambda architecture</a>, which supports unified data pipelines for batch and real-time processing.</p>\n <p>Business intelligence (<a href="https://searchbusinessanalytics.techtarget.com/definition/business-intelligence-BI">BI</a>) platforms and the ability to configure them are another important focus for data engineers. With BI platforms, they can establish connections among data warehouses, data lakes and other data sources. Engineers must know how to work with the interactive dashboards BI platforms use.</p>\n <p>Although machine learning is more in the data scientist\'s or the machine learning engineer\'s skill set, data engineers must understand it, as well, to be able to prepare data for machine learning platforms. They should know how to deploy machine learning algorithms and gain insights from them.</p>\n <p>Lastly, knowledge of <a href="https://searchdatacenter.techtarget.com/definition/Unix">Unix</a>-based operating systems (OS) is important. Unix, Solaris and <a href="https://searchdatacenter.techtarget.com/definition/Linux-operating-system">Linux</a> provide functionality and root access that other OSes -- such as Mac OS and Windows -- don\'t. They give the user more control over the OS, which is useful for data engineers.&nbsp;</p>\n <div class="youtube-iframe-container">\n  <iframe id="ytplayer-0" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/EEu5eZaIHig?autoplay=0&amp;modestbranding=1&amp;rel=0&amp;widget_referrer=https://searchdatamanagement.techtarget.com/definition/data-engineer&amp;enablejsapi=1&amp;origin=https://searchdatamanagement.techtarget.com" type="text/html" height="360" width="640" frameborder="0"></iframe>\n </div>\n <p>As the data engineer job has gained more traction, companies such as IBM and <a href="https://searchdatamanagement.techtarget.com/definition/Hadoop">Hadoop</a> vendor Cloudera Inc. have begun offering certifications for data engineering professionals. Some popular data engineer certifications include the following:</p>\n <ul class="default-list"> \n  <li><strong>Certified Data Professional</strong> is offered by the Institute for Certification of computing professionals, or ICCP, as part of its <a href="https://iccp.org/data-professionals.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">general database professional program</a>. Several tracks are offered. Candidates must be members of the ICCP and pay an annual membership fee to take the exam.</li> \n  <li><strong>Cloudera Certified Professional Data Engineer</strong> verifies a candidate\'s ability to ingest, transform, store and analyze data in Cloudera\'s data tool environment. Cloudera charges a fee for its <a href="https://www.cloudera.com/about/training/certification/ccp-data-engineer.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">four-hour test</a>. It consists of five to 10 hands-on tasks, and candidates must get a minimum score of 70% to pass. There are no prerequisites, but candidates should have extensive experience.</li> \n  <li><strong>Google Cloud Professional Data Engineer</strong> tests an individual\'s ability to use machine learning models, ensure data quality and build and design data processing systems. Google charges a fee for the <a href="https://www.dataquest.io/blog/what-is-a-data-engineer/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">two-hour, multiple choice exam</a>. There are no prerequisites, but Google recommends having some experience with Google Cloud Platform.</li> \n </ul>\n <p>As with many IT certifications, those in data engineering are often based on a specific vendor\'s product, and the trainings and exams focus on teaching people to use their software.</p>\n</section>            \n<section class="section main-article-chapter" data-menu-title="How to become a data engineer">\n <h3 class="section-title"><i class="icon" data-icon="1"></i>How to become a data engineer</h3>\n <p>Certifications alone aren\'t enough to land a data engineering job. Experience is also necessary to be considered for a position. Other ways to break into data engineering include the following:</p>\n <ul class="default-list"> \n  <li><strong>University degrees.</strong> Useful degrees for aspiring data engineers include bachelor\'s degrees in applied mathematics, computer science, physics or engineering. Also, master\'s degrees in computer science or computer engineering can help candidates set themselves apart.</li> \n  <li><strong>Online courses.</strong> Inexpensive and free online courses are a good way to learn data engineering skills. There are many useful videos on YouTube, as well as free online courses and resources, such as the following six options: \n   <ol class="default-list"> \n    <li><strong>Codecademy\'s Learn Python</strong>. <a href="https://www.codecademy.com/learn/learn-python" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Knowledge of Python</a> is essential for data engineers. This course requires no prior knowledge.</li> \n    <li><strong>Coursera\'s guide to Linux server management and security</strong><strong>. </strong>This four-week course covers the <a href="https://www.coursera.org/learn/linux-server-management-security" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Linux basics</a>.</li> \n    <li><strong>GitHub SQL Cheatsheet</strong><strong>.</strong> This GitHub repository is consistently updated with <a href="https://github.com/enochtangg/quick-SQL-cheatsheet" target="_blank" rel="noopener">SQL query examples</a>.</li> \n    <li><strong>O\'Rei</strong><strong>lly data engineering e</strong><strong>-books.</strong> Titles in the <a href="https://www.oreilly.com/data/free/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">big data architecture section</a> cover data engineering topics.</li> \n    <li><strong>Udacity D</strong><strong>ata Engineering Nanodegree</strong><strong>.</strong> Udacity\'s online learning offerings include a <a href="https://www.udacity.com/course/data-engineer-nanodegree--nd027" target="_blank" rel="noopener">data engineering track</a>.</li> \n   </ol> </li> \n  <li><strong>Project-based learning.</strong> With this more practical approach to learning data engineering skills, the first step is to set a project goal and then determine which skills are necessary to reach it. The project-based approach is a good way to maintain motivation and structure learning.</li> \n </ul>\n</section>   \n<section class="section main-article-chapter" data-menu-title="Data engineer vs. data scientist">\n <h3 class="section-title"><i class="icon" data-icon="1"></i>Data engineer vs. data scientist</h3>\n <p>Data engineers and data scientists work together. The data engineers prepare and organize the data that companies have in databases and other formats. They also build data pipelines that make data available to the data scientists. The data scientists use all that data for analytics and other projects that improve business operations and outcomes.</p>\n <p>Data scientists and data engineers differ in their skillsets and focus. Data engineers don\'t necessarily have a specific focus; they tend to be competent in several areas and well-rounded in their knowledge and skills. By contrast, data scientists often have specialized areas of focus. They are concerned with more <a href="https://searchbusinessanalytics.techtarget.com/feature/Python-exploratory-data-analysis-and-why-its-important">exploratory data analysis</a>. Data scientists tackle new, big-picture problems, while data engineers put the pieces in place to make that possible.</p>\n <figure class="main-article-image full-col" data-img-fullsize="https://cdn.ttgtmedia.com/rms/onlineimages/04_08_20_ESS_2020_4983_business_analytics_key_differences.jpg">\n  <img data-src="https://cdn.ttgtmedia.com/rms/onlineimages/04_08_20_ESS_2020_4983_business_analytics_key_differences_mobile.jpg" class="lazy" data-srcset="https://cdn.ttgtmedia.com/rms/onlineimages/04_08_20_ESS_2020_4983_business_analytics_key_differences_mobile.jpg 960w,https://cdn.ttgtmedia.com/rms/onlineimages/04_08_20_ESS_2020_4983_business_analytics_key_differences_desktop.jpg 1280w" alt="how data engineers\' and data scientists\' skills and responsibilities compare">\n  <figcaption>\n   <i class="icon pictures" data-icon="z"></i>Data engineers and data scientists have overlapping but different sets of skills and responsibilities on the data management team.\n  </figcaption>\n  <div class="main-article-image-enlarge">\n   <i class="icon" data-icon="w"></i>\n  </div>\n </figure>\n <p><em>In addition to data engineers and data scientists, data management and analytics teams contain a variety of roles and specialties. Read more about the skillsets and personnel required to have a </em><a href="https://searchbusinessanalytics.techtarget.com/feature/What-makes-up-a-strong-data-science-team-structure"><em>strong enterprise data science team</em></a><em>.</em></p>\n <div class="extra-info">\n  <div class="extra-info-inner">\n   <h4>More about data engineers and data scientists</h4> \n   <p>Data scientists and engineers are key parts of any data analytics team. Learn more about the IT pros who work together to make data analytics happen.</p> \n   <ul class="default-list"> \n    <li><a href="https://searchdatamanagement.techtarget.com/feature/USAA-adds-data-engineering-skills-to-speed-data-science-work">USAA adds data engineering skills to speed data science work</a></li> \n class="post-2178 page type-page status-publish hentry"><div class="entry-content"><p>Data engineering is the aspect of data science that focuses on practical applications of data collection and analysis. For all the work that data scientists do to answer questions using large sets of information, there have to be mechanisms for collecting and validating that information. In order for that work to ultimately have any value, there also have to be mechanisms for applying it to real-world operations in some way. Those are both engineering tasks: the application of science to practical, functioning systems.</p> <!- mfunc feat_school -><div class="fs-expanded-con fs-expanded-w-img-con"><div Program</a></div></div><div class="fs-action"> <a target="_blank" rel="nofollow" href="http://aspireclicks.com/NoodleStevensDataScienceGradProgramsFSB" class="fs-btn-e  fs-linkout-tr" Logo" width="120" height="60" src="https://images.aspireclicks.com/scranton.gif"/></noscript><img class="lazyload fs-img" alt="The University of Scranton Logo" width="120" height="60" src=\'data:image/svg+xml,%3Csvg%20xmlns=%22http://www.w3.org/2000/svg%22%20viewBox=%220%200%20120%2060%22%3E%3C/svg%3E\' data-src="https://images.aspireclicks.com/scranton.gif"/> </a><div class="fs-content"> <a target="_blank" rel="nofollow" href="https://aspireclicks.com/wScrantonDataScienceGradProgramsFSB" class="fs-title-link-e  fs-linkout-tr" data-code="UOS" data-point="title">The University of Scranton</a><div class="fs-info"><span class="fs-sub-title">Featured Program: </span><a target="_blank" rel="nofollow" href="https://aspireclicks.com/wScrantonDataScienceGradProgramsFSB" class="fs-program-link-e  fs-linkout-tr" data-code="UOS" data-point="description">Masters of Science in Health Informatics - Data Analytics</a></div></div><div class="fs-action"> <a target="_blank" rel="nofollow" href="https://aspireclicks.com/wScrantonDataScienceGradProgramsFSB" class="fs-btn-e  fs-linkout-tr" data-code="UOS" data-point="button">Request Info</a></div></div></div><div class="fs-footer-e"></div></div> <!- /mfunc feat_school -><p>Data engineers focus on the applications and harvesting of big data. Their role doesnt include a great deal of analysis or experimental design. Instead, they are out where the rubber meets the road (literally, in the <a href="https://www.wired.com/2016/09/udacity-self-driving-car-engineer-nanodegree-program-thrun/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">case of self-driving vehicles</a>), creating interfaces and mechanisms for the flow and access of information. They may be experts in:</p><ul><li>System architecture</li><li>Programming</li><li>Database design and configuration</li><li>Interface and sensor configuration</li></ul><p>Although data engineers dont always get the glory of coming up with crazy insights by querying and combining big data sources, their work is important in building the data stores that are used in that work, and in taking those insights and putting them to practical use.</p><h2>Data Engineers Are Hands-On Information Processing Professionals</h2><p>More than any other professional working in data science, data engineers have to be hands-on with the tools of the trade. A data engineer whose resume isnt peppered with references to Hive, Hadoop, Spark, NoSQL, or other high-tech tools for data storage and manipulation probably isnt much of a data engineer.</p><p>But as important as familiarity with the technical tools is, the concepts of data architecture and pipeline design are even more important. The tools are worthless without a solid conceptual understanding of:</p><ul><li>Data models</li><li>Relational and non-relational database design</li><li>Information flow</li><li>Query execution and optimization</li><li>Comparative analysis of data stores</li><li>Logical operations</li></ul><p>Data engineering is very similar to software engineering in many ways. Beginning with a concrete goal, data engineers are tasked with putting together functional systems to realize that goal.</p><p><strong><em>From Robots to Cars, Data Engineers Turn Data Science Into Useful Systems</em></strong></p><p>Data engineering has recently become prominent through ventures in autonomous vehicle design. While the servos and actual control mechanisms for self-driving cars are relatively straightforward to install and configure, the difficulty in building an autonomous car lies in duplicating the dozens of decisions made every second while using those controls:</p><ul><li>When to stop and when to go</li><li>Where to turn</li><li>How to recognize road signs and traffic controls</li><li>How to interpret the actions of other vehicles and pedestrians</li><li>What route to take from point A to point B</li></ul><p>These are all inherently data-driven decisions. While data scientists may come up with the fancy algorithms that break a map down using artificial intelligence or designing machine learning techniques to train the vehicle what a bicyclist looks like from any angle, data engineers are responsible for creating the systems to take in the sensor information from GPS, LIDAR, cameras, and motion devices, process it, and turn it into actions for the wheel, gas, and brakes of the vehicle.</p><p>Of course, data engineering has many applications outside of autonomous vehicles, as well. Like most of the field of data science, the data engineering role is still being defined and may incorporate different aspects of the job at different organizations. Data engineers may be responsible for:</p><ul><li>Data architecture</li><li>Database setup and management</li><li>Data infrastructure design and build</li></ul><p>In organizations with large amounts of data, particularly from disparate sources, all of this often boils down to building and filling up a data warehouse.</p><p><strong><em>Data Warehousing Is The Killer App For Corporate Data Engineers</em></strong></p><p>A data warehouse is a central repository of business and operations data that can be used for large-scale data mining, analytics, and reporting purposes. The warehouse allows many different data sources and repositories to be combined into a single useful tool for data scientists and business users to reference.</p><p>The process of building this resource, however, typically involves some significant extract, transform, and load (ETL, in industry parlance) operations, taking data form the source databases and reformatting it for inclusion into the warehouse. The design and coding of the processes behind the ETL operation are usually the responsibility of data engineers, as are the automation steps that are usually created at the same time to ensure a continuous data pipeline that can function without human intervention.</p><p>The organic growth of database support systems in modern businesses has made architecting and building functional data warehouses a complicated businesses indeed, and data engineers are the experts that companies turn to when its time to figure out how to get sales data from an Oracle database to talk with inventory records kept in a SQL Server cluster.</p><p>Its the responsibility of data engineers to manage and optimize these operations as well. Some understanding of the underlying server hardware is often helpful in addition to having an expert knowledge of the database software itself.</p><p>Data engineers might also be asked to create data services for other users to consume. These pipelines run in the opposite direction of those bringing information into the data warehouse. Instead, they are common APIs (Application Programming Interfaces) that provide consistent access mechanisms to backend data stores. Essentially, data engineers write translators for their data stores that use a consistent language for accessing information even when the stores themselves differ considerably.</p><h2>Learning to Be a Data Engineer</h2><p>Data engineers need just as much education for their position as any other type of data scientist. Instead of high-level information theory and advanced analytics skills, data engineers focus more on learning:</p><ul><li>Data modeling techniques</li><li>Relational and non-relational database theory and practice</li><li>Database clustering tools and techniques</li><li>ETL design</li><li>Architectural projections</li></ul><p>Although they will commonly go through regular data science masters programs, data engineers will take electives that focus more on programming skills and data storage and manipulation tools.</p><p>When entering the workforce, they will often find it beneficial to seek out certifications that are specific to the tools they plan to work with, such as Microsofts family of SQL Server-related certifications, or MongoDBs Certified Professional certification.</p><p>There are also a number of data engineering certifications however:</p><ul><li><a href="https://cloud.google.com/certification/data-engineer" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Google Cloud Data Engineer Certification</a></li><li><a href="https://www.cloudera.com/more/training/certification/ccp-data-engineer.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Cloudera Certified Professional Data Engineer</a></li><li><a href="https://www.microsoft.com/en-us/learning/mcsa-data-engineering-with-azure.aspx" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Microsoft Certified Solutions Associate in Data Engineering with Azure</a></li></ul><p>Although these are also tool-specific certifications (for Google Cloud Platform, Hadoop, and Microsoft Azure, specifically) they discuss those tools specifically from the data engineering perspective, teaching you how the systems can be used to solve data engineering problems.</p></div><footer class="entry-meta"></footer></article></div><div class="col-lg-3 col-lg-pull-9 col-sm-4 col-sm-pull-8 leftnav"><div class="leftnavcontent"><div id="leftnav"><div
